  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ea77ffb9-f3b7-4a7e-80a4-eee31ff794b5'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer13219343821380462363">The Wolves have been defeated, but our tet faces yet another catastrophe. Susannah Dean’s body has been usurped by a demon named Mia who wants to use Susannah’s mortal form to bear a demon child.   <span id="freeText13219343821380462363" style="display:none">The Wolves have been defeated, but our tet faces yet another catastrophe. Susannah Dean’s body has been usurped by a demon named Mia who wants to use Susannah’s mortal form to bear a demon child. Stealing Black Thirteen, Mia has traveled through the Unfound Door to 1999 New York where she plans to give birth to her chap, a child born of two mothers and two fathers who will grow up to be Roland’s nemesis. With the help of the time-traveling Manni, Roland and Eddie plan to follow Susannah while Father Callahan and Jake will find Calvin Tower, owner of the vacant lot where a magical rose grows: a rose that must be saved at all costs. But despite our ka-tet’s intentions, ka has its own plans. Jake, Callahan, and Jake’s bumbler companion are transported to New York to follow Susannah, while Eddie and Roland are tumbled into East Stoneham, Maine, where they are greeted by Eddie’s old enemy, the gangster Balazar. But it isn’t just bullets that Roland and Eddie must brave. Soon they will meet their maker, in the form of a young author named Stephen King.</span>

<div class='spoiler'>

<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a href="/questions/1052433-why-break-the-fourth-wall-demolished"><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Why break the fourth wall? Demolished, really. Why do that? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></a>

<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1052433'><a id="like_count_community_question_1052433" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/1052433?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">1 like</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F5093.Song_of_Susannah">like</a></span>

<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/1052433-why-break-the-fourth-wall-demolished">3 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/1052433-why-break-the-fourth-wall-demolished">See all 3 answers</a>
</li>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/1632127-sean"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1497983491i/1632127._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/1632127-sean">Sean</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I began the DT series understanding King places himself in the books at some point. When I first heard about this I assumed it was a bad idea. Breakin<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I began the DT series understanding King places himself in the books at some point. When I first heard about this I assumed it was a bad idea. Breaking the fourth wall can be a cool device, but is seldom beneficial to the story... unless you're talking about Deadpool.<br /><br />After I read this part of the story I understood King placed a slightly fictional version of himself in the books, not his true self. The idea to be conveyed here is how truly important the Dark Tower is. It's the linchpin holding together ALL worlds, including ours, where there is a Stephen King who writes the Dark Tower series. <br /><br />If I was the editor I would probably advise against this aspect of the Dark Tower series. It does take you out of the books initially and is distracting from the plot. In the end it was not as bad as I assumed it would be.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerFooter'>

<div id="review_2320519552" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2320519552" />
    <a title="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus"><img alt="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588320656p2/78485297.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2320519552?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " href="/user/show/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus">Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus?shelf=king-stephen">king-stephen</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2320519552" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3181649476919303103">After enjoying some short, not really peaceful, time together, the ka-tet has to be separated to accelerate the plot.<br/><br/>Close to everything is related to the other novels, so we have:<br/><br/>Susannah Mia is internally torn apart and a bit indecisive about the best <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[prenatal class. The idea of interworld, -dimensional- whatever crossbreeding has so many potentials for thrill that just a small variety may have already been told <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Just take all the average fantasy races, aliens, r</span>
  <span id="freeText3181649476919303103" style="display:none">After enjoying some short, not really peaceful, time together, the ka-tet has to be separated to accelerate the plot.<br /><br />Close to everything is related to the other novels, so we have:<br /><br />Susannah Mia is internally torn apart and a bit indecisive about the best <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[prenatal class. The idea of interworld, -dimensional- whatever crossbreeding has so many potentials for thrill that just a small variety may have already been told <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Just take all the average fantasy races, aliens, real animals, and mix it all up together to any result you may wish and one can imagine what storylines could be constructed that way. The characters, mentality, goals, of the different parties are as manifold and could be used for innuendos, humor, or just adding an extra layer of complexity to the already existing, biological, mental, dimensional,…uniqueness.<br /> <br />I´ve already mentioned this in the review of book 5, but I can´t overemphasize it enough: I´ve hardly ever seen an author integrating her/himself as a major plot point in a series, but King does it in a funny and self-critical way. I imagine it difficult to caricature oneself for the sake of a good story and it might be close to impossible to not lose the suspension of disbelief, something King amazingly never seems to have to worry about. It´s also a great allegory and metaphor for the power of imagination and fantasy, a love letter to the magic ability of literature to make real what seem translucent. <br /> <br />I´ve wasted much time thinking and philosophizing about what these dead trees are doing with my brain, realizing I´ve been away for years, asking myself, while remembering that we know exactly nothing about brain science, quantum physics, just everything, if I have been here or somewhere else. And if I´ve reached the unique trance state of becoming once with the story, did I live my boring meatsack life, or were I somewhere else and did this place really exist at that moment in a place we still can´t understand. But back to good old violence and gore.<br /> <br />All comes together at the end again, someone dies (you won´t expect who, believe me), and we are sadly coming closer to the end of something unique, as other authors may write as good as King, but nobody included so much of himself in her/his work. Writers may be better at worldbuilding, more dynamic, and very especially at avoiding info dumping and unnecessary lengths, but hardly someone wants or dares to share intimate details about her/himself with the world as King does. He loves reading, all of his kids are bookaholics and/or authors, and I can´t imagine how beautiful and ecstatic is must be to both read and write, especially as King describes it as leaving reality, letting the characters tell the story without much planning, turning on the music, and lifting of.<br /><br />Tropes show how literature is conceptualized and created and which mixture of elements makes works and genres unique: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Literature/SongOfSusannah">https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.ph...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3181649476919303103" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_724692051" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/724692051" />
    <a title="Bookwraiths" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14716035-bookwraiths"><img alt="Bookwraiths" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353765210p2/14716035.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/724692051?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bookwraiths" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bookwraiths" href="/user/show/14716035-bookwraiths">Bookwraiths</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14716035-bookwraiths?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14716035-bookwraiths?shelf=extra-special-authors">extra-special-authors</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer724692051" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11106592194588997380">I'm going to sit down and write reviews on the whole Dark Tower series after I finish, but I just have to say these books are becoming more and more tiresome. It just seems as if King has lost the vision of Roland the Gunslinger, so he - in order to have something to write about - constantly tinkers with the lore, changes history around, blames things on this multi-timestream concept, or spends whole novels describing an event merely to snap his fingers and change everything the next book so as </span>
  <span id="freeText11106592194588997380" style="display:none">I'm going to sit down and write reviews on the whole Dark Tower series after I finish, but I just have to say these books are becoming more and more tiresome. It just seems as if King has lost the vision of Roland the Gunslinger, so he - in order to have something to write about - constantly tinkers with the lore, changes history around, blames things on this multi-timestream concept, or spends whole novels describing an event merely to snap his fingers and change everything the next book so as to move his new plot line along. And the worst part of it all is that I've begun <i> The Dark Tower VII: The Dark Tower</i> and it appears to be in the same vein as the last two novels and not the great novels from earlier in the series. <br /><br />To me, <i>The Gunslinger</i>, <i>The Waste Lands</i> and <i>Wizard and Glass</i> were epic works, because King seamlessly combined fantasy, post-apocalyptic, horror, and - dare I say it - western themes to create something fresh and grand. Reading one of those novels was like trying out a new dessert for the first time and savoring this delicious taste you had discovered.<br /><br />On the other hand, <i>The Drawing of the Three</i>, <i>Wolves of the Calla</i>, and <i>Song of Susannah</i> read like contemporary, horror type novels, played out mainly in modern America rather than the addictive lands of Mid-World. It is just ho-hum fiction, nothing to set it apart from other books of that sort besides the title Dark Tower part whatever. <br /><br />And if the gradual unraveling of a once great story wasn't progressing fast enough, Stephen King decides to do something that is just unthinkable to me: write himself into the story as a god-creator, almost a Rose Part Deux. <br /><br />How could he have ever thought that was a good idea? <br /><br />I honestly don't know, because it did nothing to actually make sense of the growing mess that is the Dark Tower series. Perhaps it will help shape the ending, but if so, I have just went todash and have witnessed the train wreck which will be the end of the Dark Tower series. <br /><br />These are just my initial thoughts on <i>Song of Susannah</i> and the Dark Tower series as I begin reading the last book. No matter how annoyed I feel at this moment, I've made a commitment to finish the Dark Tower, so I will push forward, even though I cringe to think how bad the ending is going to be. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11106592194588997380" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_16429502" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/16429502" />
    <a title="Kara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/858991-kara"><img alt="Kara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1201816200p2/858991.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/16429502?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kara" href="/user/show/858991-kara">Kara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer16429502" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6794741982083448894">The story wasn't bad, some of the new characters were interesting, but I cannot give it a higher rating because of the author himself.<br/><br/>Stephen King has indulged in the ULTIMATE form of ego stroking in this volume and it pissed me off. The plot could've been structured some other way to avoid what he's doing right now - you *can* adjust plot, much as it sometimes hurts to do so - and the fact that he went ahead and wrote what he wrote is annoying and... well, gross. It's gross. <br/><br/>I had hoped, by the</span>
  <span id="freeText6794741982083448894" style="display:none">The story wasn't bad, some of the new characters were interesting, but I cannot give it a higher rating because of the author himself.<br /><br />Stephen King has indulged in the ULTIMATE form of ego stroking in this volume and it pissed me off. The plot could've been structured some other way to avoid what he's doing right now - you *can* adjust plot, much as it sometimes hurts to do so - and the fact that he went ahead and wrote what he wrote is annoying and... well, gross. It's gross. <br /><br />I had hoped, by the time I finished the book, that I could understand why he did it, that maybe I'd see that the story really *had* to be written that way. At the end of this book, I didn't see that and was still irked. And disappointed.<br /><br />Only one more book to go, and I'm doubting he'll redeem himself in my eyes...</span>

<div id="review_1659363714" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1659363714" />
    <a title="Johann (jobis89)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50893023-johann-jobis89"><img alt="Johann (jobis89)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588540681p2/50893023.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1659363714?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Johann (jobis89)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Johann (jobis89)" href="/user/show/50893023-johann-jobis89">Johann (jobis89)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780340827185" href="/book/show/893966.Song_of_Susannah">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1659363714" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6787855167610366213">“It got so I couldn't tell if you were the hero, the antihero, or no hero at all.”<br/><br/>The sixth book in King’s Dark Tower series, wherein the ka-tet are split up and sent to different “whens” and “wheres” to achieve their goals.<br/><br/>Song of Susannah was one of those instances where a reread proved to be very informative... as what I thought happened in this book did not actually happen in this book... I was getting ahead of myself. And for that reason I understand the complaints that not much really happ</span>
  <span id="freeText6787855167610366213" style="display:none">“It got so I couldn't tell if you were the hero, the antihero, or no hero at all.”<br /><br />The sixth book in King’s Dark Tower series, wherein the ka-tet are split up and sent to different “whens” and “wheres” to achieve their goals.<br /><br />Song of Susannah was one of those instances where a reread proved to be very informative... as what I thought happened in this book did not actually happen in this book... I was getting ahead of myself. And for that reason I understand the complaints that not much really happens in here plot-wise, it does serve as more of a build-up and a bridge to the final book in the series.<br /><br />There are three separate storylines running simultaneously as the ka-tet is divided, and all feel very fraught and tense in their own ways, but I do miss the interaction between all the characters. Susannah’s strand is probably my least favourite, which is a shame as it should be the most thrilling, but at times it felt bogged down with these hallucinations and the three voices conversing together - it wasn’t always clear what was happening.<br /><br />Not everyone is a fan of how meta the series gets, but I for one, am a fan of this! Although on this reread I did find some parts a little... cringeworthy? But I understand why King chose to write this into the story, as it makes sense in the grander scheme of his entire body of work, as a lot of it is connected to this series. (If it seems like I’m not making much sense, I am trying to remain spoiler-free for anyone who may come across this review but hasn’t got this far yet) But I know fans’ opinions vary widely on this!<br /><br />The end of the book is thrilling as everything comes to a head and we are left on an almighty cliffhanger as we proceed into the final book of the series. Song of Susannah is probably my least favourite book in the series, but there is still much to enjoy and appreciate, and I won’t be waiting too long to delve into that final book again!<br /><br />“As for you, Constant Reader... One more turn of the path, and then we reach the clearing. Come along with me, will ya not?”<br /><br />4 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6787855167610366213" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_6595563" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/6595563" />
    <a title="Kemper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/405390-kemper"><img alt="Kemper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495476851p2/405390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/6595563?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kemper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kemper" href="/user/show/405390-kemper">Kemper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781880418598" href="/book/show/644171.Song_of_Susannah">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=uncle-stevie">uncle-stevie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=dark-tower">dark-tower</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=time-travel">time-travel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=alt-universes">alt-universes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=2011-r">2011-r</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=western">western</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer6595563" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2797507400253073410"><i>“Would’ee speak a word of prayer first, Roland? To whatever God thee holds?”<br/><br/>“I hold to no God,” Roland said. “I hold to the Tower and won’t pray to that.”</i><br/><br/>Damn, I love that line. It so perfectly sums up Roland, his quest to find the Tower, what it’s cost him, and how he knows he isn’t done paying yet.<br/><br/>For years, it seemed like <i>Dark Tower</i> had been walking in aimless circles during the long breaks between the third, fourth and fifth books. We knew that King had finished the final three volumes after</span>
  <span id="freeText2797507400253073410" style="display:none"><i>“Would’ee speak a word of prayer first, Roland? To whatever God thee holds?”<br /><br />“I hold to no God,” Roland said. “I hold to the Tower and won’t pray to that.”</i><br /><br />Damn, I love that line. It so perfectly sums up Roland, his quest to find the Tower, what it’s cost him, and how he knows he isn’t done paying yet.<br /><br />For years, it seemed like <i>Dark Tower</i> had been walking in aimless circles during the long breaks between the third, fourth and fifth books. We knew that King had finished the final three volumes after losing a game of chicken with a minivan, and he’d gotten the story back up and striding briskly in the right direction with <i>Wolves of the Calla</i> including ending that one on a pretty wicked cliffhanger. <br /><br />Still the pace of this one took me by surprise. It’s like King suddenly pulled out a whip and started cracking it over the heads of the <i>DT</i> fans while screaming, “Run, you bastards! You gotta run if you want to find out what happens! BWAH-HA-HA-HA-HA!” <br /><br />And he didn’t even let us stretch properly first. That’s how you end up with a pulled hamstring.<br /><br />Susannah’s demon pregnancy led to her being taken over by the personality of Mia, and she fled Mid-World to New York in 1999 via the Doorway Cave. As Susannah wrestles Mia for control of her own body and learns more about the Crimson King, Roland and Eddie plan to follow and save her while Jake and Callahan also come to our world to protect the rose growing in a vacant lot which is actually a critical incarnation of the Tower. But when things go off the rails, all of the gunslingers will have to scramble to try and save not only Susannah, but their own lives.<br /><br />This is essentially a set-up book that preps the way for the conclusion in the last one, and it doesn’t resolve a helluva lot on it’s own. Still, I like it for its breakneck pace and the sense of urgency that King worked into this one. The breaking of a beam in Mid-World before the action moves to New York was a great reminder of the stakes here. The lines of force holding reality together are being subverted by the Crimson King’s breakers, and the so-called beamquake when one snaps is a stark warning to Roland and company that they are quickly running out of time. <br /><br />Unfortunately, while the Susannah pregnancy story makes for a pretty good hook to drive the urgency of the story, it ends up being kind of unsatisfying overall once you know how the whole series ends. Plus, the conflict between Susannah and Mia reminded me a lot of a very similar plot that King had done in <i>Dreamcatcher</i> shortly before this book was released so it didn’t seem all that fresh.<br /><br />Overall, there’s a feel of desperation in this one that takes us nicely into the final volume, and the cliffhangers here had me on the edge of my seat the first time I read this.<br /><br />There’s one controversial piece to this part of the <i>DT</i> story. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ A lot of fans don’t like that King wrote himself into this, and I was hesitant about it myself the first time through this when I wasn’t sure how the story would end. At the end of <i>Wolves of the Calla</i> and into this one, I was worried that it was going to turn out that the Dark Tower was Stephen King himself and that its fall was his ‘death’ due to the minivan accident.<br /><br />Knowing the ending now and rereading this, writing himself into the story doesn’t bother me as much. If he’d portrayed himself as some kind of all-knowing creator, I might have hated it too, but he didn‘t. He’s a pawn with a role to play. A role he kind of screws up by not getting off his ass and finishing this series sooner. <br /><br />I like that the power behind the Tower is the force of creation itself, and that the Crimson King and the other baddies are agents of chaos and destruction. I think of it as the Tower was saving itself by creating a story of a hero on a quest, and it needed someone to write that story. Enter King, who actually made himself look kind of crappy in the process. <br /><br />It’s not my favorite part of the series, but it didn’t ruin it for me either. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="2797507400253073410" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1546065835" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1546065835" />
    <a title="Jeff " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12618229-jeff"><img alt="Jeff " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529089518p2/12618229.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1546065835?book_show_action=true">Dec 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeff " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeff " href="/user/show/12618229-jeff">Jeff </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780641923456" href="/book/show/6987278-song-of-susannah">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12618229-jeff?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12618229-jeff?shelf=scifi-fantasy">scifi-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12618229-jeff?shelf=cuz-mah-fah-says-so">cuz-mah-fah-says-so</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1546065835" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2679860545572748374">Upon coming to, Stephen King registered a mixed expression of fear, anger and puzzlement. Perhaps being bound and gagged had something to do with it. His face was contorted and purple and his hair was standing up with much of it covering his forehead and bulging eyes.<br/><br/>The tall, ungainly gunslinger was standing over him, concerned and apologetic.<br/><br/>“Sorry that I hit ya, Sai. If I take off the duct tape, will ya promise that ya won’t scream?”<br/><br/>King vigorously nodded.<br/><br/>“You was running away and shoutin’ an</span>
  <span id="freeText2679860545572748374" style="display:none">Upon coming to, Stephen King registered a mixed expression of fear, anger and puzzlement. Perhaps being bound and gagged had something to do with it. His face was contorted and purple and his hair was standing up with much of it covering his forehead and bulging eyes.<br /><br />The tall, ungainly gunslinger was standing over him, concerned and apologetic.<br /><br />“Sorry that I hit ya, Sai. If I take off the duct tape, will ya promise that ya won’t scream?”<br /><br />King vigorously nodded.<br /><br />“You was running away and shoutin’ and I didn’t really know what else to do, but bop ya on the head,” the gunslinger explained as he removed the tape.<br /><br />The first thing out of King’s mouth: “Who the hell are you?” <br /> <br />“It ain’t really who I am that’s important, it’s who you are.”<br /><br />“Huh?”<br /><br />“Yer the Gan, the God, the all-creator of everything. Books you wrote about a Dark Tower have kind of bled over into different realities. I’m in one of these realities and I don’t mind tellin’ ya, things are getting mighty tough.”<br /><br />“Can you get me a beer?”<br /><br />The gunslinger groaned and limped over to the refrigerator.<br /><br />“Why the hell are you limping so badly?”<br /><br />“My nutsack is sore. It caught on the doorway when I got sucked into this here reality.”<br /><br />King stared at the gunslinger as he removed the cap from the beer and gave King a swig.<br /><br />“You’re not going to untie me, are you?”<br /><br />“Look my time is short and I’ll do it right before I leave. I gots a list here in my pocket."<br /><br />He pulled a crumpled piece of paper from his pocket and started reading, slowly.<br /><br />“First, don’t write the Dark Tower books.”<br /><br />“If I don’t write them, then won’t you disappear?”<br /><br />“How in tarnation do ya figure that, Mr. Smarypants Gan?”<br /><br />“Well, if your existence is based on the writing of those books and I don’t write them, then you won’t be around.”<br /><br />“Well, hell, just…uh…write somethin’ a little different.”<br /><br />There was a sound of off-key chimes in the distance.<br /><br />“Pardon Sai, but I have to speed this up a bit. If you got to write them, write some of them shorter. Also, don’t write books about the eyes of a dragon, Tom Gordon, a cell and…”<br /><br />The chimes were growing louder.<br /><br />“Also, if you get a visit from two blonde gunslingers, don’t listen to a word they’re sayin’. They can be very persuasive and they’ll put a hurtin’ on ya. Don’t eat no chocolate cake or drink any Kool-ade neither.”<br /><br />The chimes were now deafening.<br /><br />“Gotta go, your ganship and thankee.”<br /><br />The gunslinger limped quickly out the door.<br /><br />Suddenly, the chimes stopped.<br /><br />“You big galoot. You forgot to untie me.”<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2679860545572748374" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_14801066" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/14801066" />
    <a title="Dan Schwent" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent"><img alt="Dan Schwent" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593973948p2/870755.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/14801066?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dan Schwent" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dan Schwent" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent">Dan Schwent</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781880418598" href="/book/show/644171.Song_of_Susannah">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=reread-in-2011">reread-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=western">western</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=weird-western">weird-western</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer14801066" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17369844860727060588"><b>The 2011 re-read:</b><br/>Susanna/Mia uses Black Thirteen and flees to New York to have her baby. Roland, Eddie, Jake, and Callahan get the Manni to open the Unfound Door and end up in the wrong places. Can Roland and Eddie convince Calvin Tower to sell them the lot where the Rose grows? Can Jake and Callahan find Susannah before she has her baby?<br/><br/>Song of Susannah was my least favorite book in the Dark Tower series the first time through. Susannah has never been my favorite character in the Dark Tower sag</span>
  <span id="freeText17369844860727060588" style="display:none"><b>The 2011 re-read:</b><br />Susanna/Mia uses Black Thirteen and flees to New York to have her baby. Roland, Eddie, Jake, and Callahan get the Manni to open the Unfound Door and end up in the wrong places. Can Roland and Eddie convince Calvin Tower to sell them the lot where the Rose grows? Can Jake and Callahan find Susannah before she has her baby?<br /><br />Song of Susannah was my least favorite book in the Dark Tower series the first time through. Susannah has never been my favorite character in the Dark Tower saga and this book is really Susannah-heavy. On the second read, I had to raise it another star. The Susannah/Mia conflict had its moments and did a lot of setting up for the big shebang coming in the seventh and final book. A lot more background information was revealed.<br /><br />I'd be lying if I said Susannah was the reason I upped this one a star upon re-reading. The other reason is that Jake and Eddie seem like bonafide Gunslingers in this book, even more than they did in Wolves of the Calla. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I have a feeling their fates in The Dark Tower are going to be almost as painful the second time through. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> The relationship between Eddie and Roland has developed quite a bit since The Drawing of the Three, as has Roland's character. I still love Long, Tall, and Ugly, even though he'd probably leave me along the Path of the Beam the first morning I bitched about not having coffee.<br /><br />There is something else that I liked a lot more the second time but it's pretty spoilerific. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Now that I've had a few years to digest Stephen King writing himself into the story, it doesn't really irk me like it did the first time. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />While it's not my favorite of the Dark Tower books, it's still good and it lays a lot of the cards down on the table for the final volume, The Dark Tower. See you all along the Path of the Beam.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17369844860727060588" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2134517433" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2134517433" />
    <a title="R.K. Gold" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40737518-r-k-gold"><img alt="R.K. Gold" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518717825p2/40737518.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2134517433?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="R.K. Gold" class="user" itemprop="url" name="R.K. Gold" href="/user/show/40737518-r-k-gold">R.K. Gold</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2134517433" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4366405395756133021">And the series continues. It's something special when you read a book that has so much of the author's heart and soul laced into the pages. This series is so much a part of King that he had to make himself a character in it (that scene with King talking to Eddie Dean and Roland was something else. <br/><br/>Like with all books in the series thus far, the journey has been infinitely more important than the destination. His mind truly is an amazing thing, the way he doesnt see himself as a great architect, </span>
  <span id="freeText4366405395756133021" style="display:none">And the series continues. It's something special when you read a book that has so much of the author's heart and soul laced into the pages. This series is so much a part of King that he had to make himself a character in it (that scene with King talking to Eddie Dean and Roland was something else. <br /><br />Like with all books in the series thus far, the journey has been infinitely more important than the destination. His mind truly is an amazing thing, the way he doesnt see himself as a great architect, but a vessel for his imagination--or simply a translator for his fantasies. It's honestly the only way I could see someone constructing a universe (or a multi-verse) the way he has. Could you imagine outlining every detail of this series? How exhausting that would be--not just exhausting, in fact I think that's the wrong word altogether. Daunting. Yeah, that sounds better. If I had to outline a series like this I think I would be too intimidated to start. No wonder it was hidden in a waste box for decades in his basement, I'd be terrified to face this mammoth down too. <br /><br />Anyway, there really is something about reading a book by a great. There's just some sort of emotional stirring in your gut when you read their work, something that reminds you just what greatness is. I love this series, and I now look on to the last book sad that it's coming to an end. Don't get me wrong, I'm ready to see the Tower and follow Roland inside but I'm sad the journey is coming to a close. The good news is, there are more great books out there to read--but there's only one dark tower. </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1248648502" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1248648502" />
    <a title="Richard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8386404-richard"><img alt="Richard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351707681p2/8386404.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1248648502?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Richard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Richard" href="/user/show/8386404-richard">Richard</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780340836163" href="/book/show/815434.Song_of_Susannah">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8386404-richard?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8386404-richard?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8386404-richard?shelf=western">western</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1248648502" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2500204939645823985">7/10<br/> <br/>Well played Mr. King, well played. Very clever of you to lower my expectations going into the final book with this less than stellar attempt. Clever indeed. Now I’m not going into the final book with my expectations set at “best series finale ever!” and more hoping for “nicely wraps up the series”.<br/> <br/>Whilst not the strongest in the series (possibly the weakest, if you can really call it weak) this was still an exciting read in places. Certain parts of the story actually were really good and m</span>
  <span id="freeText2500204939645823985" style="display:none">7/10<br /> <br />Well played Mr. King, well played. Very clever of you to lower my expectations going into the final book with this less than stellar attempt. Clever indeed. Now I’m not going into the final book with my expectations set at “best series finale ever!” and more hoping for “nicely wraps up the series”.<br /> <br />Whilst not the strongest in the series (possibly the weakest, if you can really call it weak) this was still an exciting read in places. Certain parts of the story actually were really good and made for a very quick read overall. The shootout with Roland and Eddie near the beginning was one of the series highlights in fact and was truly gripping.<br /> <br />The parts I didn’t like all that much were the Mia and Susannah parts which did take up over half of the book, I found it hard to pay attention to these parts and was wishing for a quick return to some real “Gunslinging” but they were necessary for the direction of the series (I can only hope/assume). <br /> <br />It’s hard to not put series spoilers in a review of the 6th book in a series but the following may contain mild ones (be warned!). The elephant in the room is clearly the fact that Stephen King writes himself into this story. This normally grates when an author does that, like Clive Cusslar, the egotistical, self-centred prick that he is. I really disliked it when he wrote himself into “Inca Gold” and I just wanted to throw the book in the fire, the smug git. However, rant over, I actually quite liked what King was doing with this and how he met with certain characters and interacted with them in “real life”. I especially liked the Coda at the end where King was writing in a semi-biographical journal about his desire and need to return to the ka-tet for reasons unknown to himself.<br /> <br />In summary, if you’ve read the first 5 then the chances are you will read this and hopefully not be too disappointed with it. Some may even enjoy it and like what King is doing. I liked it but it definitely was not a series high and more a setup for the finale. I also noticed I’ve not rated any of the books in the series higher than 4* individually but the series as a whole is definitely 5*. A series well worth starting if you’ve not as of yet.<br /> <br />If you like this try: “11/22/63” by Stephen King</span>
  <a data-text-id="2500204939645823985" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1770096028" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1770096028" />
    <a title="Stepheny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7091879-stepheny"><img alt="Stepheny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567725280p2/7091879.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1770096028?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stepheny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stepheny" href="/user/show/7091879-stepheny">Stepheny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781880418598" href="/book/show/644171.Song_of_Susannah">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=all-hail-the-crimson-king">all-hail-the-crimson-king</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=favorite-series">favorite-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=badd-ass-fantasy">badd-ass-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=rereads">rereads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=reads-with-buddies">reads-with-buddies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=guilty-pleasure-reads">guilty-pleasure-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=pantsless-platoon">pantsless-platoon</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1770096028" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17829996585449188504"><br/>3.5 <br/><br/>Approximately 800 years ago I began a quest; a quest to take some much-loved friends of mine on a journey like no other. I enjoy doing things like this. I enjoy people reading books that I love so much I am willing to bludgeon them with said books until they agree to read them.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1489433573ra/22214570.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/> Luckily, with the Gunslinger I did not need to do too much convincing. That crazy MahFah Jeff joined on willingly enough with Delee and I. <br/><br/>(Little did he know, he’d be spending the rest of his pitiful life in my basem</span>
  <span id="freeText17829996585449188504" style="display:none"><br>3.5 <br><br>Approximately 800 years ago I began a quest; a quest to take some much-loved friends of mine on a journey like no other. I enjoy doing things like this. I enjoy people reading books that I love so much I am willing to bludgeon them with said books until they agree to read them.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1489433573ra/22214570.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> Luckily, with the Gunslinger I did not need to do too much convincing. That crazy MahFah Jeff joined on willingly enough with Delee and I. <br><br>(Little did he know, he’d be spending the rest of his pitiful life in my basement! *cackles*)<br><br>Since our journey began we have gathered and lost many. We have had some real fun times adding adverbs and adjectives to Delee’s nickname. We’ve enjoyed the company of one another and managed to not kill Dan 2.0. <br><br>Yet. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1489433573ra/22214571.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Song of Susannah is my least favorite in the series. No matter how many times I read the series through, Susannah just never grows on me. Now, could this be because she is paired with my literary soul-mate, Edward Cantor Dean? No, no. That has <i>nothing</i> to do with it…. I swear. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1489433573ra/22214572.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>*dares anyone to question her with her death-stare*<br><br>*watches Jeff flinch and cackles*<br><br>The reason I don’t like Susannah is that she continuously fucks everything up. She’s difficult. And annoying. And unnecessary. She’s just a character I don’t care for. I don't know how else to put it. Her story does not interest me. I felt like King made her a little flat. Jake, Eddie and Roland all have this wonderfully interesting backstory that draw me in. <i>Parts</i> of Susannah’s story are interesting, but every time I start to think I’m invested in her, I find she does something to make me want to punch that crazy bitch in her throat. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1489433573ra/22214573.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I try to like her, I really do. But I don’t. <br><br>Her story in this gets completely out of control and takes a turn I’ve never liked. It is probably the one aspect of the Dark Tower that I really can't get behind. (Trust me, guys, it gets worse in the last book). <br><br>After the events in Wolves of the Calla, Susannah has disappeared. She’s slipped off to the Dixie Pig to deliver her chap. That’s all you need to know. Right there. I summed up her entire story in two sentences. The rest of the book is gold. It’s Eddie and Roland off on one adventure while Pere Callahan and Jake go on another. All the while Susannah makes things worse and worse by the minute. Because she is the worst.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419803164ra/13128740.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I am excited to see the gang’s reaction to the finale-except Dan…I think Dan will hate it. (Just a feeling I have, I could be way wrong!) I am also very sad that a 3-year journey is coming to an end. When Jeff, Delee and I started this in 2014 none of us knew that it would become what it has today. I mean, shit! There are people who joined us that literally fell off the face of the Goodreads Planet never to be heard from again! And yet here we are… Me and my favorite GR people preparing to take on the final installment. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1489433573ra/22214574.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Guys, I’ll try my best to keep the tears to a minimum. No promises. But just remember:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1489432919ra/22214453.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="17829996585449188504" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily " href="/user/show/2377230-emily">Emily </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1031510776" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer529314315617978446">This book was just disgusting in it's narcissism and lack of story advancement. Once again we have a 400 page book where nothing at all really happens for 95% of the book. Also it's a book that is all about Susannah - who I have hated since I first "met" her. <br/><br/>The entire story diverges from the "rules" of the established world that has been created in all the previous books. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ Suddenly Susannah can imagine a microphone and talk to other people mind to mind? WHAT! Since when? Since w</span></span>
  <span id="freeText529314315617978446" style="display:none">This book was just disgusting in it's narcissism and lack of story advancement. Once again we have a 400 page book where nothing at all really happens for 95% of the book. Also it's a book that is all about Susannah - who I have hated since I first "met" her. <br /><br />The entire story diverges from the "rules" of the established world that has been created in all the previous books. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Suddenly Susannah can imagine a microphone and talk to other people mind to mind? WHAT! Since when? Since when has Susannah been able to have conversations with her other personalities?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I also found there to be some ridiculous plot contrivances like <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ the little turtle charm that makes a person do whatever you want.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Most egregious of all and the most supercilious is how Stephen King writes himself into the story as a character. It was beyond what I can accept or tolerate.<br /><br />The entire book was completely irritating and I'm sick to death of the overuse of the weird way everyone talks. I'm sick of a story about the Dark Tower, never actually progressing towards the Dark Tower. I'm tired of a bunch of filler books which don't advance the story. I have no idea how this series is mentioned sometimes on lists of "the best fantasy fiction".<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_2869766416" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2869766416" />
    <a title="Dan Schwent" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent"><img alt="Dan Schwent" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593973948p2/870755.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2869766416?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dan Schwent" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dan Schwent" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent">Dan Schwent</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=2019-books">2019-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2869766416&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2869766416" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16543468394299662580">In the aftermath of the battle with the Wolves, Susannah disappears with Black Thirteen to go have her baby. Can the rest of the ka-tet find Susannah and secure the vacant lot where The Rose grows before the Tower falls?<br/><br/>This is my third time reading Song of Susannah. It's still in my Dark Tower bottom three but I come at it from a different perspective since my wife and I will be greeting our chap in just under a month.<br/><br/>In my re-read of Wolves of the Callah, I said I thought that book could have </span>
  <span id="freeText16543468394299662580" style="display:none">In the aftermath of the battle with the Wolves, Susannah disappears with Black Thirteen to go have her baby. Can the rest of the ka-tet find Susannah and secure the vacant lot where The Rose grows before the Tower falls?<br /><br />This is my third time reading Song of Susannah. It's still in my Dark Tower bottom three but I come at it from a different perspective since my wife and I will be greeting our chap in just under a month.<br /><br />In my re-read of Wolves of the Callah, I said I thought that book could have been a hundred pages shorter. The same goes for Song of Susannah. There is so much extraneous crap in this! Talk, talk, talk. The Beams holding up the Dark Tower are in danger but let's waste a lot of time with chitchat. Susannah is my least favorite member of the ka-tet and this one is very Susannah-heavy.<br /><br />That being said, I still enjoy it. While I logically know the Tower isn't going to fall, King has me frantically reading to make sure this is still the case. The man knows how to ratchet up the suspense when the characters aren't talking everything to death. Eddie and Jake seem like bonafide bad asses in this book, even more than the last. There were also quite a few references I didn't catch the first time through, like to blind bluesman Reverend Gary Davis and to The Quincunx.<br /><br />I found it somewhat off-putting when Stephen King wrote himself into the series when I first read it but it seems like a normal part of the story now, like a scar that's faded so much it's almost invisible.<br /><br />Not a whole lot else for me to say, I'm afraid. This was very much a transitional book. I think maybe Stephen King wanted the Dark Tower to go seven books and padded Wolves and this one to make it so. Trimming the fat and combining Wolves and Song into one would probably have made a better reading experience.<br /><br />Okay, back on the Path of the Beam for me. Let's see if I can get to the Dark Tower before my wife gives birth to our chap.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16543468394299662580" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText1353435574778463062" style="display:none"><b> Song of Susannah </b> was not as enjoyable for me this time around. That was truly chilling. I don't remember these being in the book back when I read it the first time, so it may be something that was only included in the audio, or in reprints of the original book? If I'm in error about that, I'm sure someone will let me know. <br /><br />I only have one book to go in my audio re-read of the DT series. </span>

<div id="review_570511390" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/570511390" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/570511390?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=worldbuilding-sf">worldbuilding-sf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2020-shelf">2020-shelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer570511390" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14504464118067091489">This book is much more wonderful the second time around. Who knows, maybe it'll jump another notch by the third or the fourth. :)<br/><br/>This is a series that only gets better when you're swimming in the massive loads of details that combine Stephen King's life, the amazing worldbuilding of his bibliography, and add the little idea that Stephen King has put his SOUL into the DT.<br/><br/>What do I mean by that? Well, by his own admission, this is his magnum opus, his breathtaking, soul-stealing epic that ties tog</span>
  <span id="freeText14504464118067091489" style="display:none">This book is much more wonderful the second time around. Who knows, maybe it'll jump another notch by the third or the fourth. :)<br /><br />This is a series that only gets better when you're swimming in the massive loads of details that combine Stephen King's life, the amazing worldbuilding of his bibliography, and add the little idea that Stephen King has put his SOUL into the DT.<br /><br />What do I mean by that? Well, by his own admission, this is his magnum opus, his breathtaking, soul-stealing epic that ties together the grand majority of his separate novels and short stories and gives us a whole cosmology wrapped in an awesomely tight story that not only shits all over anyone's ideas of standard genres, but revels in breaking EVERY genre it can get its greedy little hands on.<br /><br />In other words: this is a master storyteller's story. Few writers could get away with publishing this OR getting away with all the things he gets away with.<br /><br />Do you really think that Roland is hoofing it to a huge dark tower in the distance?<br /><br />Well, yeah, he is, but first, we've got to deal with the multiverse, super high-technology with AI's, multidimensional travel, the forced entropy of every universe, and the fate of a rose, an author, a ball in a bowling bag, and the number 19. Sound strange? Well, add a shootout, car accidents, the trials of motherhood with multiple personalities, and the snickity snack of cutlery and the call for long pork!<br /><br />Does that sound strange?<br /><br />This book mostly takes place in modern New York City.<br /><br />Kinda interesting for a Ka-Tet used to a high-tech/fantasy wasteland that is really just a western, no?<br /><br />But the most interesting part is something I will not spoil for those who have not read it. This joy is a really, really big joy. The references to King's life, his works, his favorite music, and his fears are all probably the things that gave me the most shivers. The most awe. And definitely the most laughter.<br /><br />Is this series the most personal of the author's works?<br /><br />Yes. And we are Well Met. Well Met indeed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14504464118067091489" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_234635390" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/234635390" />
    <a title="Kathryn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6504379-kathryn"><img alt="Kathryn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590065910p2/6504379.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/234635390?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathryn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathryn" href="/user/show/6504379-kathryn">Kathryn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780340836163" href="/book/show/815434.Song_of_Susannah">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6504379-kathryn?shelf=stephen-king-read">stephen-king-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6504379-kathryn?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6504379-kathryn?shelf=i-recommend">i-recommend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6504379-kathryn?shelf=2012-read">2012-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6504379-kathryn?shelf=scifi-fantasy">scifi-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6504379-kathryn?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer234635390" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12618252937818331197">I just finished Song of Susannah, and it's ending has made me want to immediately dive right into the last book of The Dark Tower series, The Dark Tower. For the past few weeks while I've been reading SoS, I've really been eager to find out if Roland makes it to The Tower. Now, I'm a little sad to be starting the last book, the final journey. <br/><br/>I give SoS four stars. For me, it was a great installment, no doubt, to the series. However, I can't give it the extra star to make it a five star installm</span>
  <span id="freeText12618252937818331197" style="display:none">I just finished Song of Susannah, and it's ending has made me want to immediately dive right into the last book of The Dark Tower series, The Dark Tower. For the past few weeks while I've been reading SoS, I've really been eager to find out if Roland makes it to The Tower. Now, I'm a little sad to be starting the last book, the final journey. <br /><br />I give SoS four stars. For me, it was a great installment, no doubt, to the series. However, I can't give it the extra star to make it a five star installment for a few reasons. I believe five star books should touch the reader in a special way, or grip you unlike any other novel can. For me, The Waste Lands and Wolves of the Calla, (books 3 and 5 of The Dark Tower series) did those things to me. SoS to me felt like a book just to get you 'there,' to that last book. <br /><br />Some of the questions I had, ideas in my head, were answered or confirmed in this book. Some of the revelations, you know what I'm talking about if you've read it, made me say, "OMG!!! OH HELL TO THE NO!!" But like I said, for me it was just a 'passage to the end of the journey' type book to me.<br /><br />For some reason, Roland is a character I....identify? with or maybe I just feel like I know him, or a version of him in real life. Eddie, I feel like I know him, too. He reminds me a lot of myself in a few ways, e.g. has an older brother who used to pick on and make fun of him. The drug addiction part....ha...definitely CANNOT identify with. Jake...There's something about him, too, I identify with. He reminds me of my eight year old nephew, who is most definitely, the coolest kid I know. Maybe that is why Jake has a special place in my literary heart. Oy....well, I love animals. I have two cats of my own, and my cat Gizmo....she would definitely make The Dark Tower journey with me, or something like it if I had to go on a similar quest. Plus, he just sounds so cute and adorable. Pere Callahan, I also find to be interesting, especially his story in 'Salem's Lot and how it relates to the Dark Tower series. (Nicely done, King.)<br /><br />I tell you of my like or love for those characters for a reason: Susannah/Odetta/Detta/Mia isn't my favorite character. We're both female, but I feel like I can't really relate to her. I am definitely not saying I dislike her character, because I don't. I think she's perfect for the series. But, I feel like, hmm....maybe I just don't connect with her or identify with her like I do the others. (To me, I don't consider being female a connection. I mean, I do in some cases, but for some reason, being female doesn't make me feel connected to her, and I think identification should go deeper than that.) She definitely has an importance in this series, and King has utlized her character for many great things. Her story is interesting, too. Maybe it is my lack of identification with the character which makes this part of the journey a 4-star segment. Edit to add: I think another thing which urks me about this book, is Mia and the whole four personalities in one body. I liked it at first, but it got a little tiring to read for me, especially since the majority of the book was about Susannah. Maybe that's just me. <br /><br />Edit to add: As I was thinking about this book a moment ago, I was reminded of the scene in New York with Pere Callahan, Jake, and Oy. The street preacher with his "Gawd bombs" and "say amen" I could definitely picture in my head. He reminded me of a tele-evangelist in the south. I don't know why, but he did. The scene where Jake hits the cab car.....Oh my goodness...I remember thinking to myself: "Damn, Jake." I could picture Callahan and Jake's scenes in my head all too clearly. Eddie and Roland's part in this book was also really interesting to me. I felt like I was with them trying to convince Tower to sell the property. Roland and Eddie's story and Jake, Oy and Callahan's story in this book were my favorite parts in this book. <br /><br />I also want to bring up something else, which I'm still unsure if it was brilliant, or a little pompous of King: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ King inserting himself into this book. On one hand, I think it was a brilliant idea because of the 'universe' King has created with his books, and all of the connections his non-DT books have with the DT series, and vice versa. On the other hand, I found it a little show-offy. It's like, "Yes, we get it King. We know you are one of the masters of modern day literature, and you'll be remembered until the end of time for your literary achievements and contributions to literature. But, did you really need to go there?" Oh well....I found it a little ballsy of King. While I read the journal entries at the end of my edition, it made me wonder if King was alluding to his alcoholic and drug days when he was saying Roland and Eddie 'appeared' to him. He does talk about similar things of his writing process of this series. I wouldn't be surprised, though, if that was what he was alluding to.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I'm off to end this journey with the last book of the series. I'm eager and sad at the same time. Eager because as I have read these books, it has become more than a desire to know what Roland finds in the Dark Tower, or if he even makes it. Not all stories have happy endings. The end has become a NEED to know, though.. I'm sad, too, because I think I like this series more than I thought I would by now. For a while, Wizard and Glass, the fourth book, pissed me off to no end, and almost made me want to quit the series. Thankfully, Wolves of the Calla drew me back in. (Say thankya, sai King.) Also, I'm a little eager because I feel like I'm a little tied down in my reading with how long these books are and the series is. I shouldn't complain though. The idea/s are beyond original, they are genius. The story is eventful, interesting, and sucks you in. But again, I'm sad because I do love the characters. At least I own these books and can re-read them at anytime. Dark Tower....here I come...</span>
  <a data-text-id="12618252937818331197" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
